<speech by="#streicher">

<from>*Mr. <person refersTo="hansard_za">STREICHER</person>:</from>

<p>Mr. Speaker, I accept your ruling unreservedly. I want to point out that we on this side of the House have no objection to the suspension of the proceedings on the measure, but we lodge the strongest objection against the suspension of the proceedings on this Bill together with the proviso that the Bill will be proceeded with next session at the same stage as that at which proceedings are now suspended. That is the main criticism of this side of the House. We want to help the hon. member himself. He can suspend the proceedings on this measure and perhaps introduce a better Bill next year. It will give him and the council of his university a better opportunity to go fully into the implications of the Bill as well as the criticism expressed here and quite possibly to introduce a measure which will receive the wholehearted support of all of us. The hon. member is aware of the tremendous opposition outside to certain of the provisions of the Bill. It is for this reason that we are going to vote against the motion.</p>

</speech>

<speech by="#lawrence">

<from>Mr. <person refersTo="hansard_za">LAWRENCE</person>:</from>

<p>The hon. member for Rosettenville (Dr. Fisher) has raised a cogent point with regard to this motion before the House this afternoon, because he has pointed out that the motion stands in the name of the hon. member for Welkom (Mr. H. J. van Wyk) who is asking leave to revive this Bill next year. It seems to me that the motion, put in that crisp form, savours rather of a lottery; and this House has always been hesitant to commit itself to any form of State lottery. The lottery is whether the hon. member will be in this House to introduce the Bill next year.</p>

<p><span class="col_9367-9368" refersTo="page_1040"/>There is no difference between a game of chance and a lottery. Many hon. members in this House in the past have turned their faces resolutely against any question of a State lottery.</p>

</speech>

<speech by="#schoonbee">

<from>Mr. <person refersTo="hansard_za">SCHOONBEE</person>:</from>

<p>I will give you 100 to 1.</p>

</speech>

<speech by="#lawrence">

<from>Mr. <person refersTo="hansard_za">LAWRENCE</person>:</from>

<p>You see, Sir, how the debate degenerates when one has to deal with a question of this sort! The lottery simply is whether the hon. gentleman will be here next year or not. The hon. member over there has given me odds on that question. It seems to me that this House should not be asked to vote on a motion on the basis of laying odds as to whether the mover of the motion will be here to introduce his Bill next year. It introduces a completely foreign system in this House. We are now legislating on the basis of chance, not on the basis of certainty, not on the basis of skill, not on the basis of merit. If we were legislating on the basis of merit, the hon. member would not be back in this House next session. But we are taking a pure chance; and much as I have in the past had considerable sympathy for those hon. members who wished the Government to introduce a State lottery, I am not prepared to commit myself this afternoon to that principle in relation to the hon. member for Welkom. If I were permitted to do so I would take a point of order&#x2014;a point in limine as we would say in a court of law&#x2014; but I realize that that is not appropriate to the proceedings in this House this afternoon. But I do raise this not merely as a technical point but as a technical point with some value, namely, that I believe that it is quite wrong that an hon. gentleman, who may be in a process of transition or a process of translation, should seek to establish a vested right, when there is a doubt as to who his successor in title may be. If it is a question of leaving something to his political estate, to his successor, we might consider it on that basis. But we do not know who his successor will be, and we do not know whether his successor will be prepared to give his stamp of approval to what lies behind this motion. [Interjections.] Sir, I cannot have these flippancies. I say it is a dangerous principle, and I am not prepared to commit myself to this principle of voting for something on the basis of chance. In those circumstances I will vote against the motion.</p>

</speech>

<p><b>Question to Minister:</b></p>

<p><i>For oral reply</i>:</p>

<p>Standing over from 23 June 1961:</p>

<question by="#cope" to="#minister_of_bantu_administration_and_development">

<num>*III.</num>

<from>Mr. COPE</from>

<p>to ask the Minister of Bantu Administration and Development:</p>

<ol>

<li>(1) Whether any members of the Matlala tribe near Pietersburg have been removed from their Reserve since 1950; if so, (a) what are their names, (b) on what date was each removed, (c) to what place was each sent and (d) for what reasons was each removed;</li>

<li>(2) whether their cases have been reviewed each year; if so, with what result; and</li>

<li>(3) whether any have been allowed to return to their homes; if so, (a) what are their names and (b) on what date did they return?</li>

</ol>

</question>

<p><span class="col_9371" refersTo="page_1042"/><i>(Extract from Government Gazette No. 25, dd. 27th June, 1961.)</i></p>

</debateSection>

<debateSection name="#proclamation">

<heading>PROCLAMATION</heading>

<p>By the State President of the Republic of South Africa</p>

<p>Prorogation and Summoning of Parliament</p>

<p>UNDER and by virtue of the power and authority vested in me by section <i>twenty-five</i> of the Republic of South Africa Constitution Act, 1961. I hereby prorogue Parliament until Friday, the Nineteenth day of January, 1962, and I declare that the Second Session of the First Parliament of the Republic of South Africa will commence at Cape Town on that day for the dispatch of business.</p>

<p>Given under my Hand and the Seal of the Republic of South Africa at Pretoria on this Twenty-seventh day of June, One Thousand Nine Hundred and Sixty-one.</p>

<p>C. R. SWART, State President.</p>

<p>By Order of the State President-in-Council.</p>

<p>H. F. VERWOERD.</p>

</debateSection>

</debateSection>

<p><b>CHAIRMAN AND DEPUTY-CHAIRMAN&#x2014; (Rulings and Observations by)&#x2014;</b></p>

<ul>

<li>Additional Estimates (<i>see</i> &#x201C;Committee on Additional Estimates &#x201D;).</li>

<li>Amendments (<i>see</i> &#x201C; Bills &#x201D;).</li>

<li>Bills&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Amendments&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>May not be discussed if ruled out of order, 8624.</li>

<li>May not be moved&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>If an alternative amendment to amendment under consideration, 1468.</li>

<li>If an alternative clause to clause under consideration, 7261.</li>

<li>If destructive of principle of Bill as read a Second Time, 7144.</li>

<li>If incomplete in form, 8845.</li>

<li>If it extends scope of Bill, 8618.</li>

<li>If it introduces new and important principle not contemplated at Second Reading, 2235, 4022, 8864.</li>

<li>If it involves increased expenditure, 2110.</li>

<li><span class="col_81" refersTo="page_1123"/>If it renders clause unintelligible, 9357.</li>

<li>If not in one of official languages, 9121, 9123.</li>

<li>If similar in substance to amendment previously negatived, 1695-6, 1699.</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Clauses of&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Alternative, cannot be moved until clause under consideration negatived, 7261.</li>

<li>Discussion confined to clause or amendment under consideration, 1367, 7130, etc.</li>

<li>Principles of, cannot be discussed in Committee, 4035, 4036, 4042, 8795, 8796, 8835, 9157, 9294, 9295, 9336.</li>

<li>Words of enactment, not put in Committee, 4148.</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Closure&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Acceptance of, in discretion of Chair, 2655.</li>

<li>Can be moved at any time, 2655.</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Committee of Supply&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Budget debate not to be continued in, 3076, 3082, 5499.</li>

<li>Discussion confined to details of Votes or Heads before Committee, 3076.</li>

<li>Half hour speeches in, time for asking for, 4265.</li>

<li>Increased expenditure cannot be proposed, 5248.</li>

<li>Legislation, matters involving, may not be discussed in, 2626, 3082, 4939, 5464-5, 5496, 6499.</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Committee on Additional Estimates&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Discussion confined to details of Votes before Committee or to reasons for increases on respective Votes, 2163, etc.</li>

<li>Must be considered after reference to Committee by House, 2671.</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Debate&#x2014;

<ul>

<li>Newspapers, quotations from (<i>see under</i> &#x201C; Newspapers &#x201D;).</li>

</ul></li>

<li>Member must abide by and not circumvent ruling of Chair, 1696, 2502, 4224, 4795, 7336, 8835, 9156.</li>

<li>Member must address Chair, 4800.</li>

<li>Member must not argue with Chair, 2502, 5674, 7418.</li>
